    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle G}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f5f3c8921a3b352de45446a6789b104458c9f90b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.827ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle G}"></span> are equivalent, <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle H\equiv G}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>H</mi>
        <mo><!--  --></mo>
        <mi>G</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H\equiv G}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b9e71967307091f580bf9f1dbf11686037db3242" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.989ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle H\equiv G}"></span>, and the duals are strongly isomorphic: <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle H^{*}\cong G^{*}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msup>
          <mi>H</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mo><!--  --></mo>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mo><!--  --></mo>
        <msup>
          <mi>G</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mo><!--  --></mo>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{*}\cong G^{*}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/531f660e661ac4653ccd4ba2278b0ec8ebea230a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:9.137ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="{\displaystyle H^{*}\cong G^{*}}"></span>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Symmetry">Symmetry</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hypergraph&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Symmetry"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The <i><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1238216509">.mw-parser-output .vanchor>:target~.vanchor-text{background-color:#b1d2ff}@media screen{html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .vanchor>:target~.vanchor-text{background-color:#0f4dc9}}@media screen and (prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .vanchor>:target~.vanchor-text{background-color:#0f4dc9}}</style><span class="vanchor"><span id="rank"></span><span class="vanchor-text">rank</span></span></i> <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle r(H)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>r</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>H</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle r(H)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8b6cfadf9aef5e32d5c67475d841b732f032ca09" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.922ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle r(H)}"></span> of a hypergraph <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle H}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>H</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/75a9edddcca2f782014371f75dca39d7e13a9c1b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.064ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle H}"></span> is the maximum cardinality of any of the edges in the hypergraph.  If all edges have the same cardinality <i>k</i>, the hypergraph is said to be <i>uniform</i> or <i>k-uniform</i>, or is called a <i>k-hypergraph</i>.  A graph is just a 2-uniform hypergraph.
</p><p>The degree <i>d(v)</i> of a vertex <i>v</i> is the number of edges that contain it. <i>H</i> is <i>k-regular</i> if every vertex has degree <i>k</i>.
</p><p>The dual of a uniform hypergraph is regular and vice versa.
</p><p>Two vertices <i>x</i> and <i>y</i> of <i>H</i> are called <i>symmetric</i> if there exists an automorphism such that <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \phi (x)=y}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi><!--  --></mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mi>y</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \phi (x)=y}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/917214b3730f776942078819f5294dd45a663450" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:8.778ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \phi (x)=y}"></span>.  Two edges <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle e_{i}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>e</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle e_{i}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ebdc3a9cb1583d3204eff8918b558c293e0d2cf3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.883ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle e_{i}}"></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle e_{j}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>e</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>j</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle e_{j}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/64afd228cf00e5024b9cdd277462d24ab97b6d3e" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:1.993ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="{\displaystyle e_{j}}"></span> are said to be  <i>symmetric</i> if there exists an automorphism such that <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \phi (e_{i})=e_{j}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi><!--  --></mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>e</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>e</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>j</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \phi (e_{i})=e_{j}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/deb5605d10a1f327f8d3fb77679fe8c35fcea2c4" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:10.17ex; height:3.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \phi (e_{i})=e_{j}}"></span>.
</p><p>A hypergraph is said to be <i>vertex-transitive</i> (or <i>vertex-symmetric</i>) if all of its vertices are symmetric. Similarly, a hypergraph is <i>edge-transitive</i> if all edges are symmetric. If a hypergraph is both edge- and vertex-symmetric, then the hypergraph is simply <i>transitive</i>.
</p><p>Because of hypergraph duality, the study of edge-transitivity is identical to the study of vertex-transitivity.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Partitions">Partitions</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hypergraph&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Partitions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A partition theorem due to E. Dauber<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> states that, for an edge-transitive hypergraph <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle H=(X,E)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>H</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>E</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H=(X,E)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a6b45f3b01656aea8afd2786abe31e83f4643830" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.761ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle H=(X,E)}"></span>, there exists a <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_a_set" title="Partition of a set">partition</a>
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle (X_{1},X_{2},\cdots ,X_{K})}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

            <mn>1</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>X</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mo><!--  --></mo>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>X</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>K</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (X_{1},X_{2},\cdots ,X_{K})}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/faac1811025df0eee829c13e703c1fb7f5645964" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:17.596ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle (X_{1},X_{2},\cdots ,X_{K})}"></span></dd></dl>
<p>of the vertex set <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle X}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>X</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/68baa052181f707c662844a465bfeeb135e82bab" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.98ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle X}"></span> such that the subhypergraph <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle H_{X_{k}}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>H</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <msub>
              <mi>X</mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>k</mi>
              </mrow>
            </msub>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H_{X_{k}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fc393b870d503666c120456865ddea51e4ea0af9" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:4.384ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle H_{X_{k}}}"></span> generated by <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle X_{k}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>X</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>k</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X_{k}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/33c25229c6989c235f9cbb7908331f6d01d0abfe" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.013ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle X_{k}}"></span> is transitive for each <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle 1\leq k\leq K}">
  <semantics>

        <mi>k</mi>
        <mo><!--  --></mo>
        <mi>K</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle 1\leq k\leq K}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3229ff22b7f6ad15424c311b4afded2386201fea" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:10.637ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="{\displaystyle 1\leq k\leq K}"></span>, and such that
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle \sum _{k=1}^{K}r\left(H_{X_{k}}\right)=r(H)}">

        <munderover>

          </mrow>

          </mrow>
        </munderover>
        <mi>r</mi>
        <mrow>
          <mo>(</mo>
          <msub>
            <mi>H</mi>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <msub>
                <mi>X</mi>

                  <mi>k</mi>
                </mrow>
              </msub>

  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/26f61fd14944b3e1c3f724467517e1a77166ec4d" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:19.711ex; height:7.343ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \sum _{k=1}^{K}r\left(H_{X_{k}}\right)=r(H)}"></span></dd></dl>
<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle r(H)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>r</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>H</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle r(H)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8b6cfadf9aef5e32d5c67475d841b732f032ca09" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.922ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle r(H)}"></span> is the rank of <i>H</i>.
</p><p>As a corollary, an edge-transitive hypergraph that is not vertex-transitive is bicolorable.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Graph_partitioning" class="mw-redirect" title="Graph partitioning">Graph partitioning</a> (and in particular, hypergraph partitioning) has many applications to IC design<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Parallel_computing" title="Parallel computing">parallel computing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Efficient and scalable <a href="/wiki/Graph_partition" title="Graph partition">hypergraph partitioning algorithms</a> are also important for processing large scale hypergraphs in machine learning tasks.<sup id="cite_ref-hyperx_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hyperx-7"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>

.ambox{margin:0 10%}}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .ambox{display:none!important}}</style><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>One possible generalization of a hypergraph is to allow edges to point at other edges. There are two variations of this generalization. In one, the edges consist not only of a set of vertices, but may also contain subsets of vertices, subsets of subsets of vertices and so on <i>ad infinitum</i>. In essence, every edge is just an internal node of a tree or <a href="/wiki/Directed_acyclic_graph" title="Directed acyclic graph">directed acyclic graph</a>, and vertices are the leaf nodes. A hypergraph is then just a collection of trees with common, shared nodes (that is, a given internal node or leaf may occur in several different trees). Conversely, every collection of trees can be understood as this generalized hypergraph. Since trees are widely used throughout <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a> and many other branches of mathematics, one could say that hypergraphs appear naturally as well. So, for example, this generalization arises naturally as a model of <a href="/wiki/Term_algebra" title="Term algebra">term algebra</a>; edges correspond to <a href="/wiki/Term_(logic)" title="Term (logic)">terms</a> and vertices correspond to constants or variables.
</p><p>For such a hypergraph, set membership then provides an ordering, but the ordering is neither a <a href="/wiki/Partial_order" class="mw-redirect" title="Partial order">partial order</a> nor a <a href="/wiki/Preorder" title="Preorder">preorder</a>, since it is not transitive. The graph corresponding to the Levi graph of this generalization is a <a href="/wiki/Directed_acyclic_graph" title="Directed acyclic graph">directed acyclic graph</a>. Consider, for example, the generalized hypergraph whose vertex set is <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle V=\{a,b\}}">
  <semantics>

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6891318887f7a2f273818e7d9958de8a55c7e504" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.963ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle e_{2}=\{a,e_{1}\}}"></span>. Then, although <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle b\in e_{1}}">

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/11f8c068e9fa139ae9a526e4448ad415b31af218" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:5.976ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle b\in e_{2}}"></span>.  However, the <a href="/wiki/Transitive_closure" title="Transitive closure">transitive closure</a> of set membership for such hypergraphs does induce a <a href="/wiki/Partial_order" class="mw-redirect" title="Partial order">partial order</a>, and "flattens" the hypergraph into a <a href="/wiki/Partially_ordered_set" title="Partially ordered set">partially ordered set</a>.
</p><p>Alternately, edges can be allowed to point at other edges, irrespective of the requirement that the edges be ordered as directed, acyclic graphs. This allows graphs with edge-loops, which need not contain vertices at all. For example, consider the generalized hypergraph consisting of two edges <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle e_{1}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>e</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>1</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle e_{1}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6e81caf3d4bcb929315801cbabc83543829484ee" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.138ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle e_{1}}"></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\displaystyle e_{2}}">

    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle e_{2}}</annotation>
  </semantics>

  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>e</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">{</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>e</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>1</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">}</mo>

    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle e_{2}=\{e_{1}\}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f5d9c11ed556ceafdd981f8281e8a5eb1b0a0f61" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:9.699ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle e_{2}=\{e_{1}\}}"></span>. As this loop is infinitely recursive, sets that are the edges violate the <a href="/wiki/Axiom_of_foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Axiom of foundation">axiom of foundation</a>.  In particular, there is no transitive closure of set membership for such hypergraphs.  Although such structures may seem strange at first, they can be readily understood by noting that the equivalent generalization of their Levi graph is no longer <a href="/wiki/Bipartite_graph" title="Bipartite graph">bipartite</a>, but is rather just some general <a href="/wiki/Directed_graph" title="Directed graph">directed graph</a>.
</p><p>The generalized incidence matrix for such hypergraphs is, by definition, a square matrix, of a rank equal to the total number of vertices plus edges. Thus, for the above example, the <a href="/wiki/Incidence_matrix" title="Incidence matrix">incidence matrix</a> is simply

<li id="cite_note-42"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-42">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222"><cite id="CITEREFHarary2018" class="citation book cs1">Harary, F. (2018) [1969]. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=AmhQDwAAQBAJ"><i>Graph Theory</i></a>. CRC Press. p.&nbsp;172. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-429-96231-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-429-96231-8"><bdi>978-0-429-96231-8</bdi></a>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20230204155708/https://books.google.com/books?id=AmhQDwAAQBAJ">Archived</a> from the original on 2023-02-04<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2021-06-12</span></span>. <q>We next state a theorem due to Elayne Dauber whose corollaries describe properties of line-symmetric graphs. Note the obvious but important observation that every line-symmetric graph is line-regular.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Graph+Theory&amp;rft.pages=172&amp;rft.pub=CRC+Press&amp;rft.date=2018&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-429-96231-8&amp;rft.aulast=Harary&amp;rft.aufirst=F.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DAmhQDwAAQBAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHypergraph" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222"><cite id="CITEREFKarypis,_G.,_Aggarwal,_R.,_Kumar,_V.,_and_Shekhar,_S.1999" class="citation cs2">Karypis, G., Aggarwal, R., Kumar, V., and Shekhar, S. (March 1999), "Multilevel hypergraph partitioning: applications in VLSI domain", <i>IEEE Transactions on Very Large Scale Integration (VLSI) Systems</i>, <b>7</b> (1): <span class="nowrap">69</span>79, <a href="/wiki/CiteSeerX_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="CiteSeerX (identifier)">CiteSeerX</a>&nbsp;<span class="id-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://citeseerx.ist.psu.edu/viewdoc/summary?doi=10.1.1.553.2367">10.1.1.553.2367</a></span>, <a href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1109%2F92.748202">10.1109/92.748202</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=IEEE+Transactions+on+Very+Large+Scale+Integration+%28VLSI%29+Systems&amp;rft.atitle=Multilevel+hypergraph+partitioning%3A+applications+in+VLSI+domain&amp;rft.volume=7&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.pages=69-79&amp;rft.date=1999-03&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fciteseerx.ist.psu.edu%2Fviewdoc%2Fsummary%3Fdoi%3D10.1.1.553.2367%23id-name%3DCiteSeerX&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1109%2F92.748202&amp;rft.au=Karypis%2C+G.%2C+Aggarwal%2C+R.%2C+Kumar%2C+V.%2C+and+Shekhar%2C+S.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHypergraph" class="Z3988"></span><span class="cs1-maint citation-comment"><code class="cs1-code">{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Citation" title="Template:Citation">citation</a>}}</code>:  CS1 maint: multiple names: authors list (<a href="/wiki/Category:CS1_maint:_multiple_names:_authors_list" title="Category:CS1 maint: multiple names: authors list">link</a>)</span></span>
